All Reviews

  1. I own the QT4014 - Used this baby for nearly a year now and it's still going strong. While I don't aim for the bushy beard style (for now), I wouldn't doubt its capability of trimming it nice and clean. I have my settings around 3-3.5, use it at least once a week (along with a razor for the extra hair on the neck), spend a minute or two, and it keeps me at a perfectly smooth scruff that people compliment me on. People seem to complain about the shape, power switch, noise, whatever. I found no problems with any. I found the shape to be just fine as it makes the shavings less likely to fall all over your hands, and it is even better used for the neck area (just raise your head and enjoy the massage). I would assume it fairs just as well for my bearded friends. It is a little noisy, just a tiny bit, but that was never my concern since it's a proud reminder that a man is simply grooming himself. As for power, It seems to run just fine for a while without charging. I think I've charged it maybe 4 or 5 times in the past 10 months, and only one of those times seemed like it needed a charge. I'm not going to over extend, just buy this thing already. I recommend getting the Philips Norelco NT9130 D-Finer Precision Trimmer along with this for the more precise work, such as hair reaching the lips, uneven levels, eyebrows, etc. Both serve well together.
  2. I've always used the smaller hair clippers for my beard, my brother bought one and recommended it. I purchased it and have received it about a month ago. It has the dial in the middle to adjust sizes, the whole top part comes apart for easy cleaning. No batteries, just has the wall charger which saves me on buying batteries. I love this thing, and would recommend it for any guy who likes to keep the stubble or a shorter facial hair look.
  3. Great item, but the adjustable head flexes and might not give you the accurate length in .5mm increments. But overall its good enough
  4. bought this for the sole purpose to trim my arm hairs and add a sort of &#34;fade&#34; effect to my arm hair(having just cut line from bald to hair is horrible and you should not do that to yourself) so i can be hairless from my shoulders to about my elbows and the rest just neatly trimmed.<br /><br />this product definitely does the job and then some.<br /><br />easy to use, easy to clean product.

  229. I honestly don't know how this item has received so many high-star ratings! Maybe if the only thing you are using this for is to trim your head or if you have a big scruffy beard, then perhaps it might be useful and that's the only reason I am giving it 2 stars instead of 0 (or 1 the minimum allowed).<br /><br />Here's the thing, I bought this trimmer to use as a body &#34;man-scaping&#34; trimmer. DO NOT, under any circumstances, use this product for that! Especially down there! The problem lies in the design of the &#34;guide&#34;. It attaches to the unit on the back of the device, opposite side of the cutting edge. So the part that covers the cutting edge is essentially floating in the air above the cutters. Simple Physics 101 dictates then that ANY amount of pressure applied at the tip (where the razors are) is going to cause the guide to pivot at the back where it is attached. Imagine you stand up straight and hold one arm out at a 90 degree angle to you. If someone pushes downwards on your shoulder, your hand isn't going to move, but the slightest amount of pressure applied downwards on your fingertips, will cause your hand to move downwards as well while your shoulder (the fulcrum) will remain fixed. What does all this mean?! Well, with the dial on this thing turned to 3 or 3.5 or lower, the guide is pretty much useless because the guide tip will duck down when slightly pressed against your skin to the same level as the cutting razor! I learned that the VERY hard way!<br /><br />To make matters worse, the flat end of the guide, which is the part placed against the surface of your skin, is very thick, i.e., there's a ton of surface area. Placing all this surface area against your skin causes alot of friction. This results in the razor not moving in the direction you intend, so naturally, you apply a bit more pressure to get it to move and before you know it, you've applied too much and, well, see problem 1 above!<br /><br />I am giving credit forthe fact that the idea of not having to have all the little different sized guides lying around is phenomenal. But the execution of that idea for this device was an epic fail! Again, if you're just trimming back a massive amount of head hair or beard, then this thing might work OK even though I don't see anyway to get a consistent trim if it is completely dependent on the amount of pressure you apply, but whatever, i'm trying to give them a little bit of credit. But for anything else, this product is completely useless!

I am sure you are thinking duh! Trust me, I met plenty of people that needed that told to them.<br />-A bristle brush IMHO is the best way to clean this thing. Remove the guide, do a few swipes of the clipper with a brush and it's clean. The guide just rinse off and let it air dry before installing it back in the clippers.<br />-What if I lose the guide? Really you are going to lose that guide? How about paying attention to what you are doing.<br />-It does hold a charge more than long enough with the amount of use I get out of it. In fact, I yet to charge it a second time since the time of purchase and that was literally months ago.<br />-The only thing better than this for the pubic region is the Wahl Peanut due to it's size/convenience especially for men.<br /><br />That should cover it. This review is based on a few things and in no particular order:<br />1. Questions I seen on Amazon<br />2. Personal experiences with manscaping; I learned what NOT to do<br />3. Having used this model<br /><br />If you want some more info about me and my qualifications, in my early 20's due to complaints from a certain someone getting hair in a certain place I decided to start manscaping. For awhile used scissors but for all the obvious reasons I knew there had to be a better way. As soon as I heard of a person manscaping with a beard trimmer I had to try it. First time doing it I found it to be very easy and better results in comparison to scissors. The big thing was to be careful in certain areas and before this model I never went lower than a #4 but on this model I been doing #2 setting with no issues.<br /><br />Also, a &#34;hair trimmer&#34; versus a &#34;beard trimmer&#34; is night and day especially when you are talking about guides. For instance a #4 on a hair trimmer versus a beard trimmer has a significant difference. So if you want to trim your beard, back, front, or groin stick to a beard trimmer.<br /><br />Wahl Peanut by design is a tiny little unit so when you are dealing with obstacles it's convenient. However, I didn't buy the battery unit, I went with the one that must be plugged in. Not a big deal but requires a minute or more of prep work plus an extension cord so I can trim in places of my home where I don't need to worry about the hair that falls. That is where this thing comes in; you can grab and trim at a moments notice as long as the battery power is there.<br /><br />That is the other thing that kept me from returning to battery powered clippers for awhile is how the battery units usually are dead when you need them the most. Now that I have the plug-in Wahl it's not a big deal, plus this thing being able to charge in 1-hour is a huge plus too.<br /><br />Also, since I got this thing at a discount it was a no brainer.   577. The Philips Norelco QT4014 trimmer is similar to other models on the market but has several tweaks.<br /><br />First, it's a bit smaller and lighter than most and is much easier to grip and manipulate. The weight is well-balanced and it feels good in the hand.<br /><br />The length adjusting mechanism is very ergonomic with silicone strips and the wheel is accessible from the front and back so that both the thumb and forefinger can be used to to turn it very intuitively. The recesses also accomodate the fingers while using the trimmer. This is an outstanding feature.<br /><br />Similarly, the on-off mechanism is a ridged, sliding panel that is effortless. Again, very intuitive and a vast improvement on similar models.<br /><br />The cutting length is adjustable in 20 increments from 0.5 mm to 10 mm.<br /><br />The comb stays put while in use but is much easier to remove and insert for cleaning than is usual.<br /><br />It charges quickly, has an indicator light, and the converter is interchangeable with several other Philips Norelco trimmers.<br /><br />As far as negatives:<br /><br />It is slightly louder than average though not nearly in the loudest quintile.<br /><br />While the comb and blade are easily removed for washing, the unit itself cannot be exposed to water. As with most similar devices, frequent cleaning is critical for good performance and being able to rinse off the cavity under the blade would be a nice feature.<br /><br />The trimming blade is 1.5\\" wide which works well in a limited and sharply-curved area such as the face (as marketed) but of course it wouldn't be as ideal for other body parts. It's not intended as a shaver, either.<br /><br />Overall, a very nice little little beard and stubble trimmer that stands out from similar models for ease of use and handling.

Not too big or small, just the right size, in my opinion.<br /><br />(4) Looks good. Some models out there just look cheap.<br /><br />(5) No stand, just plug a cord in.<br /><br />(6) Low noise, as quiet as you can expect for a trimmer.<br /><br />CONS:<br />------<br /><br />(1) It is quite difficult to get an even length trim with an electric trimmer alone if your goal is a close trim, especially on the neck with all the long hairs that lay flat. This is likely due to the DIFFERENT ANGLES OF ATTACK, DIFFERENT PRESSURE, and DIFFERENT HAIR ANGLES FROM FACE as we move over the face and neck. If you can keep this in mind and keep it under control you might just get a more barber-ish even trim. I have not mastered this yet.<br /><br />I'm wording it this way because I'm not so sure it is the fault of this razor or its guard, it seems to be a somewhat universal complaint by a percentage of users out there for most electric trimmers.<br /><br />NOTES:<br />-------<br /><br />- I use this mostly to make actually shaving easier.
